```plaintext
*Prepared in the tiered-rigor style of the TEP/Entrodynamics central reference. Comments, corrections, and pushback welcome.*

```
```plaintext
================================================================================
ISO-PURITY TRANSPORT AND THE BLOCH VELOCITY BOUND AT d_S = 2
================================================================================


A standalone technical note documenting the derivation, proof, and honest 
placement of the bound |v| <= 2 Delta_psi(H) on the total Bloch velocity of a 
qubit reduced state under bipartite unitary evolution. Prepared as a companion 
to the TEP Tier 1.1 purity speed limit paper, capturing material that did not 
fit there but is worth preserving for future reference and possible d >= 3 
generalization.




================================================================================
1. PURPOSE AND STATUS OF THIS NOTE
================================================================================


This note documents an investigation into iso-purity transport at d_S = 2 — the 
question of what (if any) dynamics on a qubit reduced state exist orthogonally 
to purity change under bipartite unitary evolution. The investigation proceeded 
in three stages:


   (i)  Numerical exploration establishing that iso-purity transport exists, is 
        non-trivial at d_S = 2, and is bounded by a state-independent constant.
   (ii) Analytical reduction to a matrix inequality ||A - A†||_F^2 <= 2, proven 
        by direct parameterization in the Schmidt basis.
  (iii) Recognition that the resulting bound |v| <= 2 Delta_psi(H) is a direct 
        consequence of the Mandelstam-Tamm inequality applied to the optimal 
        direction observable — making it not a new theorem but a specific 
        instantiation of an existing result.


We record the work in this order because the derivation — though its endpoint 
coincides with an immediate MT corollary — contains structural content worth 
preserving: an explicit Schmidt-basis form for the saturating perpendicular 
state, a constructive characterization of saturating Hamiltonians, and a 
clarification of the relationship between iso-purity transport and the 
dimension d_S = 2 specifically.


Epistemic status: the bound |v| <= 2 Delta_psi(H) is proven (Tier 1). Its 
identification as a consequence of MT is straightforward (Tier 1). The 
discussion of what the constructive proof adds beyond MT (Section 7) is a 
methodological observation (Tier 2). Open questions in Section 10 are Tier 3.




================================================================================
2. THE QUESTION
================================================================================


The TEP Tier 1.1 bound governs the rate of change of the reduced-state 
spectrum via a single spectral functional:


   |d gamma / dt|  <=  4 ||H|| sqrt(F),     F := p_3 - gamma^2


At d_S = 2, one might initially suspect that this bound encompasses all 
non-trivial dynamics of rho_S — after all, a qubit spectrum (lambda, 1-lambda) 
is determined by a single number, so it is tempting to conflate "moves the 
reduced state" with "moves gamma". This suspicion is wrong: iso-purity 
transport at d_S = 2 exists and can be substantial, corresponding to 
eigenvector rotation of rho_S at fixed spectrum.


Three questions organize the investigation:


   (a) Does iso-purity transport exist at d_S = 2?
   (b) If so, how fast can it proceed — is there a complementary bound on the 
       perpendicular component of the Bloch velocity?
   (c) What is the structural character of iso-purity transport at d_S = 2, 
       and how does it relate to the rank-2 bivector W of the TEP framework?


We answer all three: yes, |v_perp| <= 2 ||H|| at d_S = 2, and iso-purity 
transport at d_S = 2 is pure eigenvector rotation (no moment-change component, 
since all spectral moments are gamma-determined at d_S = 2).




================================================================================
3. NUMERICAL EXPLORATION
================================================================================


Setup: fix a pure global state |psi> = sqrt(p)|00> + sqrt(1-p)|11> in Schmidt 
form. The reduced state rho_S = diag(p, 1-p) has Bloch vector r = (0, 0, 
2p-1), purity gamma = (1 + r^2)/2. Sample 10^5 random Hermitian Hamiltonians 
H on C^2 tensor C^2, normalized to ||H|| = 1, and compute the Bloch velocity 
v = dr/dt of the reduced state. Extract v_|| = v . r-hat (parallel component, 
drives gamma-change) and v_perp = v - v_|| r-hat (perpendicular component, 
iso-purity).


Findings:


   - Iso-purity transport exists. Many Hamiltonians yield |d gamma / dt| 
     approximately 0 while |v_perp| is order unity.


   - The maximum iso-purity rate is state-independent. Across p in {0.55, 
     0.65, 0.75, 0.85, 0.95}, random sampling yields max|v_perp| approximately 
     1.7-1.9; subsequent multi-start Nelder-Mead optimization yields 
     max|v_perp| = 2.000 to four decimal places, independent of p.


   - The maximum total Bloch velocity is 2 ||H||. Optimization confirms 
     max|v| = 2.000 for every tested Schmidt parameter including p = 0.5 
     (maximally entangled) and p = 0.99 (nearly product), as well as three 
     generic (non-Schmidt-form) random pure states.


   - Individual component maxima are not jointly achievable. At the 
     Hamiltonian maximizing v_||, v_perp is approximately 0; at the 
     Hamiltonian maximizing v_perp, v_|| is approximately 0; the sum of 
     squared individual maxima (7.00 at p = 0.75) is strictly larger than 
     max|v|^2 = 4.00.


The state-independence of max|v| was not expected at the outset. A 
system-local Hamiltonian on rho_S alone gives max|v| = 2|r| ||H_S||, which 
is state-dependent (zero at r = 0, the maximally-mixed fixed point). But 
bipartite Hamiltonians acting non-trivially across the S-E boundary achieve 
the state-independent max|v| = 2 ||H||, demonstrating that bipartite coupling 
removes the r-dependent "braking" of the reduced-state rotation.




================================================================================
4. ANALYTICAL SETUP
================================================================================


Fix a pure global state |psi> and a Hermitian Hamiltonian H with <psi|H|psi> 
= c. Decompose H|psi> into its parallel and orthogonal parts relative to 
|psi>:


   H|psi>  =  c |psi>  +  Delta |psi_perp>


where Delta = Delta_psi(H) = sqrt(<psi|H^2|psi> - c^2) is the energy variance 
on |psi> and |psi_perp> is a unit vector orthogonal to |psi>. Then


   [H, |psi><psi|]  =  H |psi><psi|  -  |psi><psi| H
                    =  (c|psi> + Delta|psi_perp>)<psi|  -  |psi>(c<psi| + Delta<psi_perp|)
                    =  Delta ( |psi_perp><psi|  -  |psi><psi_perp| )


The c-terms cancel because c is real (H Hermitian). Apply the partial trace 
over E:


   d rho_S / dt  =  -i Tr_E [H, |psi><psi|]  =  -i Delta (A - A†)


where A := Tr_E |psi_perp><psi| is an operator on the 2-dim Hilbert space 
H_S. Note A - A† is anti-Hermitian, so -i(A - A†) is Hermitian — as required 
for d rho_S / dt.


The Frobenius norm:


   || d rho_S / dt ||_F  =  Delta · || A - A† ||_F


The Bloch velocity: rho_S = (I + r . sigma)/2, so d rho_S / dt = (1/2) v . 
sigma, which gives


   || d rho_S / dt ||_F^2  =  (1/4) sum_k v_k^2 · ||sigma_k||_F^2  =  |v|^2 / 2


Therefore |v| = sqrt(2) · || d rho_S / dt ||_F, and


   |v|  =  sqrt(2) · Delta · || A - A† ||_F


To prove |v| <= 2 Delta, it suffices to show || A - A† ||_F^2 <= 2.


Preliminary check: the commutator Frobenius norm.
   
   || [H, |psi><psi|] ||_F^2  =  Tr( (A-A†)†(A-A†) ) · Delta^2 ... ? 


No, more directly: since [H, |psi><psi|] = Delta · (|psi_perp><psi| - 
|psi><psi_perp|), an anti-Hermitian operator with specific structure,


   || [H, |psi><psi|] ||_F^2
     =  Delta^2 · Tr ( (|psi><psi_perp| - |psi_perp><psi|)(|psi_perp><psi| - |psi><psi_perp|) )
     =  Delta^2 · ( <psi_perp|psi_perp><psi|psi> - <psi_perp|psi><psi_perp|psi>
                    - <psi|psi_perp><psi|psi_perp> + <psi|psi><psi_perp|psi_perp> )


The cross terms vanish by orthogonality <psi|psi_perp> = 0; the diagonal 
terms are each 1 by normalization. So


   || [H, |psi><psi|] ||_F^2  =  2 Delta^2.


A naive bound on d rho_S / dt via the partial trace: in general, 
||Tr_E X||_F <= sqrt(d_E) ||X||_F (Cauchy-Schwarz on the E-sum). For d_E = 2, 
this gives ||d rho_S / dt||_F <= sqrt(2) sqrt(2 Delta^2) = 2 Delta, 
equivalently |v| <= 2 sqrt(2) Delta. This is loose by a factor of sqrt(2) 
relative to the tight bound proved below; the slack reflects that the naive 
partial-trace bound doesn't exploit the specific anti-Hermitian structure of 
[H, |psi><psi|].




================================================================================
5. PROOF THAT ||A - A†||_F^2 <= 2
================================================================================


Use Schmidt form |psi> = sqrt(p) |00> + sqrt(q) |11> with q = 1 - p. Write 
|psi_perp> in the computational basis {|00>, |01>, |10>, |11>}:


   |psi_perp>  =  a |00>  +  b |01>  +  c |10>  +  d |11>


with a, b, c, d in C.


Constraints:


   (C1) Normalization: |a|^2 + |b|^2 + |c|^2 + |d|^2 = 1
   (C2) Orthogonality to |psi>: <psi_perp|psi> = sqrt(p) a-bar + sqrt(q) d-bar 
        = 0. Splitting into real and imaginary parts:
           Re(d) = -sqrt(p/q) Re(a)
           Im(d) = -sqrt(p/q) Im(a)
        So |d|^2 = (p/q) |a|^2, and (C1) becomes |a|^2 / q + |b|^2 + |c|^2 = 1.


Computing A entry-by-entry. In the convention A_ij = <psi_j^E | psi_perp^i> 
where |psi> decomposes as sum over i of |i>_S ⊗ |psi_i^E> with |psi_0^E> = 
sqrt(p) |0>, |psi_1^E> = sqrt(q) |1>:


   A  =  [ [ sqrt(p) a,  sqrt(q) b ],
           [ sqrt(p) c,  sqrt(q) d ] ]


Compute ||A - A†||_F^2 directly. Writing a = a_r + i a_i (and similarly for 
b, c, d), and using (C2) to write d_r = -sqrt(p/q) a_r, d_i = -sqrt(p/q) a_i:


(A - A†)_{00} = sqrt(p) (a - a-bar) = 2 i sqrt(p) a_i
(A - A†)_{11} = sqrt(q) (d - d-bar) = 2 i sqrt(q) d_i = -2 i sqrt(p) a_i
(A - A†)_{01} = sqrt(q) b - sqrt(p) c-bar
(A - A†)_{10} = sqrt(p) c - sqrt(q) b-bar


Frobenius norm squared:
   ||A - A†||_F^2  =  |2i sqrt(p) a_i|^2  +  |2i sqrt(q) d_i|^2
                    +  |sqrt(q) b - sqrt(p) c-bar|^2
                    +  |sqrt(p) c - sqrt(q) b-bar|^2


   =  4 p a_i^2  +  4 q d_i^2  +  (q |b|^2 - 2 sqrt(pq) Re(b c) + p |c|^2)
                                +  (p |c|^2 - 2 sqrt(pq) Re(c b) + q |b|^2)


Using d_i^2 = (p/q) a_i^2 and combining:


   ||A - A†||_F^2  =  8 p a_i^2  +  2 q |b|^2  +  2 p |c|^2  -  4 sqrt(pq) Re(bc)


Bounds on the free parameters:
   - a_i^2 <= |a|^2 = q (1 - |b|^2 - |c|^2), achieved when a is purely imaginary.
   - Re(bc) >= -|b| |c|, achieved when arg(b) + arg(c) = pi (anti-aligned phases).


Substituting optimal (and writing x = |b|, y = |c|):


   ||A - A†||_F^2  <=  8 p q (1 - x^2 - y^2)  +  2 q x^2  +  2 p y^2  +  4 sqrt(pq) x y
                   =:  g(x, y)


with domain x, y >= 0, x^2 + y^2 <= 1 (from |a|^2 >= 0).


Maximize g. Reparameterize x = R cos theta, y = R sin theta for R in [0,1], 
theta in [0, pi/2]:


   g  =  8 p q (1 - R^2)  +  R^2 [ 2 q cos^2 theta  +  2 p sin^2 theta 
                                    +  2 sqrt(pq) sin 2 theta ]
      =  8 p q (1 - R^2)  +  R^2 · h(theta)


where the theta-dependent factor simplifies via p + q = 1 and the double-angle 
identities:


   h(theta)  =  (p + q)  +  (q - p) cos 2theta  +  2 sqrt(pq) sin 2theta
             =  1  +  (q - p) cos 2theta  +  2 sqrt(pq) sin 2theta


Maximizing h over theta:


   max_theta h(theta)  =  1  +  sqrt( (q - p)^2  +  4 p q )
                      =  1  +  sqrt( p^2 - 2 p q + q^2 + 4 p q )
                      =  1  +  sqrt( (p + q)^2 )
                      =  1  +  1  =  2.


So max_theta h(theta) = 2 for all p in (0, 1).


Now maximize g over R: g(R) = 8 p q (1 - R^2) + R^2 · h_max, which is a 
weighted average of 8 p q (at R = 0) and h_max = 2 (at R = 1). Since p q <= 
1/4 (with equality at p = q = 1/2), we have 8 p q <= 2, so the weighted 
average is maximized at R = 1:


   max g  =  h_max  =  2.


Therefore ||A - A†||_F^2 <= 2 with equality achievable. QED.


Corollary (the Bloch velocity bound).


   |v|  =  sqrt(2) · Delta_psi(H) · ||A - A†||_F  <=  sqrt(2) · Delta_psi(H) · sqrt(2)
        =  2 · Delta_psi(H)  <=  2 ||H||


with equality in the first inequality when ||A - A†||_F = sqrt(2) (optimal 
|psi_perp> per the proof above) and equality in the second when H has a 
spectrum centered such that Delta_psi(H) = ||H||.




================================================================================
6. HONEST PLACEMENT: THIS IS MANDELSTAM-TAMM
================================================================================


The bound |v| <= 2 Delta_psi(H) follows in three lines from the Mandelstam-
Tamm inequality.


Mandelstam-Tamm: for any Hermitian observable A, 


   |d <A> / dt|  <=  2 Delta(A) · Delta(H).


Apply this to the direction observable A_n = sigma . n-hat ⊗ I_E for an 
arbitrary unit vector n-hat in R^3. Since (sigma . n-hat)^2 = I, we have


   Delta_psi(A_n)^2  =  <A_n^2>_psi  -  <A_n>_psi^2  =  1  -  (r . n-hat)^2  <=  1


with equality when n-hat is perpendicular to r. Therefore


   |d <A_n> / dt|  =  |n-hat . (dr/dt)|  =  |n-hat . v|  <=  2 sqrt(1 - (r . n-hat)^2) Delta_psi(H)  <=  2 Delta_psi(H).


Maximizing the left side over unit n-hat gives max|n-hat . v| = |v|; the 
right side is maximized at n-hat perpendicular to r, giving the universal 
value 2 Delta_psi(H). So


   |v|  <=  2 Delta_psi(H).


This is MT applied to the worst-case direction observable; the geometric 
content is already present in MT, merely repackaged in Bloch coordinates. The 
identification does not require any of the Schmidt-basis machinery of Section 5.




================================================================================
7. WHAT THE CONSTRUCTIVE PROOF ADDS
================================================================================


Given that the bound follows directly from MT, one might ask why the 
Schmidt-basis proof of Section 5 is worth preserving at all. Three reasons, 
in increasing order of utility:


(a) Explicit characterization of saturating states.
    The MT derivation gives the bound but does not, by itself, identify the 
    Hamiltonian or global state that achieves saturation. The Schmidt-basis 
    proof identifies |psi_perp> explicitly: at saturation the a-component is 
    purely imaginary (a = i |a|), and the b, c components have anti-aligned 
    phases (Re(bc) = -|b||c|), parameterized by (|b|, |c|) on the unit 
    circle. This gives a 2-parameter family of optimal |psi_perp> states, 
    each of which determines a corresponding saturating Hamiltonian (up to 
    global phase and centering).


(b) Explicit verification of saturability at every p.
    The MT derivation establishes 2 Delta_psi(H) as an upper bound, but does 
    not immediately show that bipartite Hamiltonians on C^2 ⊗ C^2 are rich 
    enough to actually achieve this bound for every choice of |psi>. The 
    Schmidt-basis proof shows max ||A - A†||_F^2 = 2 uniformly in p, 
    establishing state-independent saturability.


(c) Pathway to d_S >= 3 generalization.
    The MT-per-direction argument is specific to the Bloch-vector geometry of 
    a qubit reduced state. For d_S >= 3, the relevant generators are the 
    SU(d_S) generators (a (d_S^2 - 1)-dim basis of traceless Hermitians), and 
    the direction-observable approach requires careful handling of the 
    non-commutativity of these generators. The Schmidt-basis proof structure 
    generalizes: |psi_perp> has d_S d_E - 1 complex components, the A matrix 
    is d_S x d_S, and the optimization problem is higher-dimensional but 
    amenable to the same approach. Whether max ||A - A†||_F^2 remains a 
    state-independent constant at d_S >= 3 is open; even if it does, the 
    interpretation changes because the reduced state has spectral invariants 
    beyond gamma.




================================================================================
8. RELATION TO THE TEP BOUND
================================================================================


The TEP Tier 1.1 bound |d gamma / dt| <= 4 ||H|| sqrt(F) and the 
Bloch-velocity bound |v| <= 2 Delta_psi(H) are logically independent 
inequalities. Both must hold simultaneously; neither is a specialization or 
refinement of the other.


8.1. Different objects.


The TEP bound is a statement about a spectral functional of rho_S:
   - State-side factor: sqrt(F(rho_S)) depends only on the spectrum of rho_S.
   - Energy-side factor: ||H|| (operator norm of H).


The Bloch bound is a statement about the full variance of H:
   - State-side factor: sqrt(1 - (r . n-hat)^2), maxed at 1.
   - Energy-side factor: Delta_psi(H) (energy variance on the pure global state).


These live in different coordinate systems on the problem.


8.2. Different vanishing conditions.


TEP vanishes when F = 0. This occurs at the spectral fixed points of rho_S: 
gamma = 1/d_S (maximally mixed) and gamma = 1 (pure). Neither condition 
implies the state is static under dynamics; rather, both imply that the 
spectrum cannot change instantaneously (though eigenvectors still can).


Bloch bound vanishes when Delta_psi(H) = 0. This occurs when |psi> is an 
eigenstate of H, which trivially implies no state evolution at all.


These are genuinely different conditions; a state can have F > 0 but 
Delta_psi(H) = 0 (if H is chosen with |psi> as an eigenstate) or Delta_psi(H) 
> 0 but F = 0 (if rho_S is at a spectral fixed point).


8.3. Non-combinability into a tighter joint bound.


Write v = v_|| r-hat + v_perp, with v_|| = v . r-hat and v_perp the 
perpendicular component. Then |v|^2 = v_||^2 + |v_perp|^2, and the two 
bounds project as:


   TEP bound:    v_||^2  <=  (4 sqrt(F) ||H|| / r)^2  =  4 (1 - r^2) ||H||^2
                 (using |d gamma / dt| = r v_||, and F = r^2 (1 - r^2)/4 at 
                 d_S = 2)
   Bloch bound:  v_||^2  +  |v_perp|^2  <=  4 Delta_psi(H)^2  <=  4 ||H||^2


One might hope to combine these to extract a bound on |v_perp| alone: from 
the Bloch bound, |v_perp|^2 <= 4 Delta^2 - v_||^2, and substituting the TEP 
upper bound on v_||^2 would give |v_perp|^2 <= 4 Delta^2 - 4(1 - r^2) ||H||^2, 
or even tighter forms. This substitution is invalid. The TEP bound is an 
upper bound on v_||^2, not a lower bound; substituting it into the sum-
constraint 4 Delta^2 - v_||^2 gives a weaker, not stronger, bound on 
|v_perp|^2. (Numerically: at r = 0.1 the proposed bound would give 
|v_perp|^2 <= 0.04 ||H||^2, but actually max|v_perp| approximately 1.8 ||H||, 
a factor-of-9 violation.)


The correct structural statement is that the feasible region in (v_||, 
v_perp) space is the intersection of:
   - the TEP strip: |v_|| | <= 2 sqrt(1 - r^2) ||H||
   - the Bloch disk: v_||^2 + |v_perp|^2 <= 4 Delta_psi(H)^2


Both constraints are active in different regimes. At the TEP-saturating H, 
v_|| is maximal and v_perp is small; at the Bloch-saturating H, v_perp is 
near 2 Delta_psi(H) and v_|| is small.


8.4. Sum of squared individual maxima overcounts.


At r = 0.5, p = 0.75:
   - max v_|| over H (TEP saturating) = 2 sqrt(1 - r^2) = sqrt(3) ≈ 1.732
   - max |v_perp| over H (Bloch saturating) = 2 (independent of r)
   - Sum of squared individual maxima = 3 + 4 = 7
   - Actual max |v|^2 = 4


The gap (7 vs 4) quantifies the trade-off: the two maxima are not 
simultaneously achievable. The TEP-saturating H puts all of its 
commutator-energy into the parallel (spectrum-changing) direction; the 
Bloch-saturating H puts all of it into the perpendicular (eigenvector-
rotation) direction.




================================================================================
9. ISO-PURITY AT d_S = 2: PHYSICAL INTERPRETATION
================================================================================


At d_S = 2, the reduced state rho_S is parameterized completely by its 
3-dimensional Bloch vector r. The purity gamma = (1 + r^2)/2 depends only on 
|r|, so dynamics of rho_S splits into:


   - Radial: changes |r|, hence changes gamma. One-dimensional.
   - Angular: changes r-hat at fixed |r|. Two-dimensional (the tangent plane 
     to the Bloch sphere of radius r).


At d_S = 2, the full moment hierarchy p_k = Tr(rho_S^k) is determined by 
gamma alone (since the spectrum has only two values summing to 1). So angular 
motion at d_S = 2 preserves not just gamma, but every spectral moment — and 
hence the full spectrum. Angular motion at d_S = 2 is therefore pure 
eigenvector rotation.


This clarifies how to read the TEP framework's rank-2 bivector structure at 
d_S = 2. The framework describes W as a rank-2 antisymmetric matrix on R^d, 
and refers to the (d - 2)-dimensional orthogonal complement of W in the 
antisymmetric matrix space as containing "purity-invisible moment-changing 
modes". At d = 2, this complement has dimension d - 2 = 0: there are no 
moment-changing iso-purity modes, as the preceding paragraph established.


But iso-purity motion itself is non-trivial at d = 2, occupying 2 of the 3 
Bloch-vector directions. The resolution is that these 2 directions are 
eigenvector rotations rather than moment changes: they rotate |a> and |1-a> 
within H_S without changing (lambda_0, lambda_1). The W-complement 
dimensionality counts moment-changing modes only, and correctly reports 0 at 
d = 2; the eigenvector-rotation modes live in a separate space (the tangent 
space to the unitary orbit of rho_S, which has dimension d_S^2 - d_S = 2 at 
d_S = 2).


At d_S >= 3, the structure splits into three pieces:
   - 1 direction: W-itself, the rank-2 plane that changes gamma. 
     Bounded by TEP.
   - (d_S - 2) directions: moment-changing iso-purity modes (change higher 
     moments p_3, p_4, ... while preserving gamma). Not bounded by TEP 
     directly; a separate analysis is needed.
   - (d_S^2 - d_S) directions: eigenvector rotations at fixed spectrum. 
     Bounded by the reduced-state velocity bound (which at d_S >= 3 may have 
     a different state-independent or state-dependent constant).


A complete kinematic description of reduced-state dynamics at d_S >= 3 would 
require characterizing all three pieces. The work here handles the first 
(TEP) and last (Bloch velocity) directly at d_S = 2; the middle piece does 
not exist at d_S = 2.




================================================================================
10. OPEN QUESTIONS AND LIMITATIONS
================================================================================


10.1. Generalization to d_S >= 3.


The bound |v| <= 2 Delta_psi(H) does not obviously generalize as stated, 
because the Bloch-vector parameterization is specific to d_S = 2. For d_S >= 
3, the reduced state lives in the (d_S^2 - 1)-dim space of Hermitian 
traceless operators, and the analog of |v| is the norm of the tangent 
vector in that space. The Schmidt-basis proof structure extends: |psi_perp> 
has d_S d_E - 1 complex components, A is d_S x d_S, and the analog of 
||A - A†||_F^2 is an optimization over a higher-dimensional constraint 
manifold. Whether this optimum is state-independent (2, as at d_S = 2) or 
state-dependent at d_S >= 3 is open.


Plausible conjecture (not proven): max ||A - A†||_F^2 = 2 at d_S >= 3 with 
d_E = d_S for bipartite pure states, by the same Schmidt-basis structure. But 
this needs to be verified.


10.2. Mixed initial states.


The proof assumes pure rho_tot (so that the orthogonality |psi_perp> 
perpendicular to |psi> is well-defined). For mixed rho_tot, the analog 
replaces Delta_psi(H) with the SLD (symmetric logarithmic derivative) 
variance, and the commutator [H, rho_tot] no longer has the simple 
|psi_perp><psi| - h.c. structure. The MT extension to mixed states is 
standard; the corresponding Schmidt-basis generalization should go through, 
perhaps with adjusted constants.


10.3. Non-unitary dynamics.


Under CPTP (Lindbladian) evolution, rho_tot does not remain pure from a pure 
initial state, so the framework of Section 4 breaks. A complete treatment 
would require either (a) Stinespring-dilating the CPTP map to unitary 
evolution on a larger Hilbert space and applying the bound there, with 
constants adjusted for the dilation, or (b) a direct derivation of an 
iso-purity bound for Lindbladian dynamics. Neither has been attempted here.


10.4. Relation to channel additivity.


The TEP framework conjectures a connection between the rank-2 bivector W and 
the additivity gap of quantum channels (specifically, that the gap is bounded 
by 2 sqrt(2) - 2). Whether the iso-purity rotation modes play any role in 
this conjectured bound is unclear; they do not appear in W itself, but they 
do affect the achievable channels (since any CPTP map can be dilated to 
unitary evolution involving both W-directions and iso-purity modes).


10.5. Lie-algebraic structure of optimal Hamiltonians.


The Schmidt-basis proof identifies a 2-parameter family of |psi_perp> states 
at saturation. The corresponding Hamiltonians form a family of rank-?? 
generators on C^2 ⊗ C^2. Characterizing this family Lie-algebraically (e.g., 
as a homogeneous space of SU(4) by some stabilizer) might reveal additional 
structure.




================================================================================
11. SUMMARY
================================================================================


The bound |v| <= 2 Delta_psi(H) on the Bloch velocity of a qubit reduced 
state under bipartite unitary evolution from a pure global state is 
established via two independent routes:


   (a) Directly from Mandelstam-Tamm applied to the optimal direction 
       observable: |n-hat . v| <= 2 sqrt(1 - (r . n-hat)^2) Delta_psi(H), 
       maxed over n-hat perpendicular to r.
   (b) Via Schmidt-basis decomposition: expanding [H, |psi><psi|] = 
       Delta(|psi_perp><psi| - h.c.), tracing out E to get d rho_S / dt 
       = -i Delta (A - A†), and proving max ||A - A†||_F^2 = 2 by direct 
       parameterization and optimization.


Route (a) is immediate and establishes the bound as a consequence of MT; it 
provides no new kinematic content beyond MT itself. Route (b) is longer but 
yields three useful by-products: an explicit characterization of saturating 
states, state-independent saturability verification, and a template for d_S 
>= 3 generalization.


The bound is logically independent of the TEP Tier 1.1 purity speed limit. 
Neither implies the other; both must hold simultaneously; their individual 
maxima are achieved at different Hamiltonians and cannot be combined into a 
tighter joint constraint by simple algebraic substitution.


At d_S = 2, iso-purity transport is pure eigenvector rotation of rho_S; 
moment-changing iso-purity modes do not exist because all spectral moments 
are gamma-determined at d_S = 2. This is a dimensional specialization of the 
more general d_S >= 3 picture, where iso-purity transport splits into 
moment-changing and eigenvector-rotating pieces.




================================================================================
APPENDIX A: NUMERICAL PROTOCOLS
================================================================================


All numerics in this note were generated via direct matrix computation in 
numpy and scipy.optimize.


Sampling protocol (Section 3). For each Schmidt parameter p in {0.55, 0.65, 
0.75, 0.85, 0.95}:
   1. Generate random Hermitian H on C^4 via symmetrization of a Gaussian 
      complex matrix.
   2. Normalize to ||H|| = 1 via operator-norm division.
   3. Compute d rho_S / dt = -i Tr_E ([H, |psi><psi|]) via direct block-matrix 
      partial trace.
   4. Extract v = (Tr(sigma_1 d rho_S / dt), ..., Tr(sigma_3 d rho_S / dt)).
   5. Decompose v = v_|| r-hat + v_perp; record |v_|| |, |v_perp|, |v|.
   6. Accumulate maxima over 10^5 samples.


Optimization protocol. For more precise bounds, use scipy.optimize.minimize 
with Nelder-Mead over a 16-parameter real representation of Hermitian 4 x 4 
matrices. Multi-start with 15 random initial conditions. Results to 4-6 
decimal places.


Verified results:
   - max |v| / Delta_psi(H) = 2.000 for Schmidt p in {0.5, 0.6, 0.75, 0.9}, 
     three random pure states, the product state |00>, and the Bell state.
   - max ||A - A†||_F^2 = 2.000 for Schmidt p in {0.5, 0.6, 0.75, 0.9} under 
     constraints (C1) and (C2).
   - max g(x, y) = 2.000 for Schmidt p in {0.5, 0.6, 0.75, 0.9} under x, y 
     >= 0, x^2 + y^2 <= 1.


These three verifications are consistent, as expected from the proof chain.




================================================================================
APPENDIX B: NOTATION
================================================================================


   rho_tot          Total state on H_S ⊗ H_E.
   rho_S            Reduced state on H_S (= Tr_E rho_tot).
   |psi>            Pure global state (rho_tot = |psi><psi|).
   |psi_perp>       Unit vector orthogonal to |psi>, with H|psi> = c |psi> 
                    + Delta |psi_perp>.
   H                Hermitian Hamiltonian on H_S ⊗ H_E.
   ||H||            Operator norm (largest absolute eigenvalue).
   Delta_psi(H)     Energy variance on |psi>: sqrt(<H^2>_psi - <H>_psi^2).
   gamma            Reduced purity: Tr(rho_S^2).
   p_k              k-th spectral moment: Tr(rho_S^k).
   F                Gap functional: p_3 - gamma^2.
   r                Bloch vector of rho_S: rho_S = (I + r . sigma)/2.
   v                Bloch velocity: dr/dt.
   v_||, v_perp     Parallel and perpendicular components of v relative to r.
   A                Tr_E |psi_perp><psi|, the reduced bivector.
   p, q             Schmidt coefficients: |psi> = sqrt(p) |00> + sqrt(q) |11>,
                    q = 1 - p.
   sigma_k          Pauli matrices (k = 1, 2, 3).
   ||X||_F          Frobenius norm: sqrt(Tr(X† X)).




================================================================================
END OF NOTE
================================================================================
```
```plaintext
# Complete Record of TEP Framework Development
## Conversation Arc: February 7–16, 2026

### Document Scope

This document records the complete sequence of advancements, findings, falsifications, and reassessments made across approximately 30 conversation sessions spanning February 7 through February 16, 2026. The material is drawn from ~15,000+ lines of conversation transcripts archived at `/mnt/transcripts/`.

The arc traces a path from initial critical review of the TEP framework, through quantum geometry validation, dimensional second law testing, Casimir/conjugacy analysis, strategic assessment, spectral moment hierarchy discovery, literature review, GMC-purity identification, Fisher geometry and rank-2 transport structure, channel additivity connections, holonomy testing, and finally a rigorous novelty assessment against the existing literature.

---

# PHASE I: FRAMEWORK REVIEW AND INITIAL VALIDATION (Feb 7)

## Session 1: Critical Review of TEP Framework
**Transcript:** `2026-02-07-01-04-01-tep-framework-critical-review.txt` (254K)
**Date:** February 7, 2026

### Context
Will submitted the complete TEP (Terminal Equivalence Principle) framework document (~8,600 lines, plus supplementary documents on Boltzmann bulk constraint) for rigorous peer-level critical assessment. The request was explicit: hypervigilant interdisciplinary review with ground truth as the primary goal, not diplomacy or encouragement.

### The TEP Framework (as submitted)
The framework centers on the budget equation:

$$x^2 + u = 1$$

derived from information-theoretic constraints (passivity, boundedness, Schur complementarity). The key variables:
- **x**: signal/coherence parameter (related to purity)
- **u**: uncertainty/noise parameter (related to decoherence)
- **G(x) = 1/√(1-x²)**: the "gamma factor" — a Lorentz-like divergence at the boundary x → 1

The framework claims structural isomorphisms (not mere analogies) between:
- Network theory (impedance, scattering matrices, wye-delta transforms)
- Quantum information (purity, entanglement, decoherence)
- Relativity (Lorentz factors, horizons, time dilation)
- Thermodynamics (entropy production, equilibration)

### Key supplementary documents reviewed:
1. **Constraining the TEP Bulk by Uniqueness of Distribution** — argument that Boltzmann interior + boundary observables canonically identify the bulk
2. **Main framework document** — Parts I–IX covering budget derivation, passive holography, network theory, quantum geometry, touchstones

### Initial Assessment
The reviewer identified:
- The budget equation x² + u = 1 is mathematically well-defined
- The G-factor divergence structure is real and appears across domains
- The network theory (Schur complement, DtN maps) is rigorous
- Structural parallels between domains are genuine, not forced
- **BUT:** The critical question is whether these parallels are isomorphisms (deep) or analogies (shallow) — this requires testing specific quantitative predictions

---

## Sessions 2–4: Quantum Geometry Validation
**Transcripts:** Three sessions of `tep-quantum-geometry-validation.txt` (628K, 962K, 428K)
**Date:** February 7, 2026 (spanning ~6 hours)

### What was tested and validated:

#### 1. Rapidity Additivity
The TEP rapidity η = arctanh(x) is additive under composition of subsystems:

$$\eta_{AB} = \eta_A + \eta_B$$

This was proved analytically for product states and verified numerically. The additivity follows from the multiplicativity of purity: γ(ρ₁ ⊗ ρ₂) = γ(ρ₁)·γ(ρ₂), and the logarithmic structure of rapidity.

#### 2. Purity Speed Limit (initial version)
The first version of what would become the central result:

$$|d\gamma/dt| \leq C \cdot \gamma \cdot \sqrt{1-\gamma}$$

was tested extensively with zero violations found. The form γ√(1-γ) has the structure x·σ = x·√u in budget variables — the geometric mean of signal and uncertainty.

#### 3. Bures Metric Curvature
Computed the sectional curvature of the Bures metric on the space of density matrices. Found:
- The curvature varies with purity
- There exists a crossover point where purity metric and Bures metric curvatures balance
- For d=2 (qubits): crossover at γ* ≈ 0.586 ≈ 2 - √2

#### 4. Dimensional Thresholds
The metric crossover point γ* depends on dimension d:
- d=2: γ* = 2 - √2 ≈ 0.5858
- d=3: different value
- d→∞: approaches 1/d (maximally mixed)

The d=2 value γ* = 2 - √2 lives in the algebraic ring Z[√2], connecting to the silver ratio δ_S = 1 + √2 and octagonal symmetry.

#### 5. DHO (Damped Harmonic Oscillator) Correspondence
The mapping between quantum purity dynamics and damped oscillator parameters was tested:
- ω (frequency) ↔ coherent oscillation rate
- Γ (damping) ↔ decoherence rate
- Q = ω/Γ ↔ ratio of coherent to incoherent dynamics

The correspondence is structural: both are governed by the same quadratic characteristic equation with the budget constraint determining the discriminant.

#### 6. Coupled Oscillator Commensurability
Tested whether the Fibonacci/golden ratio structure predicted by TEP appears in coupled oscillator systems. Found preliminary evidence for φ-scaling in certain coupling regimes, but this remained speculative.

### Key insight from this phase:
The reviewer noted that p₃ (third spectral moment) appeared naturally in the purity speed limit analysis, and that this quantity captures spectral dispersion invisible at the purity level. This would become the central theme of the next two weeks.

### The qubit metric crossover
A significant finding: for qubits, the expression 4√(p₃ - γ²) simplifies to 2√2·√((2γ-1)(1-γ)), which implies p₃ = (3/2)γ - 1/2 for d=2. This exact relation between p₃ and γ is a qubit-specific identity that does not generalize to higher dimensions.

The "spherical-looking" qutrit range (1/3 ≤ γ ≤ 1/2) was identified as particularly interesting — the Bures off-diagonal curvature sweeps through a linear regime there despite enormous dynamic range in other curvature measures.

---

# PHASE II: DIMENSIONAL STRUCTURE AND CONJUGACY (Feb 8–9)

## Session 5: Dimensional Second Law Tests
**Transcript:** `2026-02-08-14-59-45-dimensional-second-law-tests.txt` (340K)
**Date:** February 8, 2026

### The Dimensional Second Law Claim
TEP predicts that composition alone (without dynamics or probability) creates a Hilbert space structure dominated by irreversible degrees of freedom. Quantitatively, the entanglement dimension ratio:

$$R_{\text{ent}} = \frac{(d_A - 1)(d_B - 1)}{d_A \cdot d_B - 1}$$

measures the fraction of the composite state space that supports entanglement.

### Tests performed:

#### 1. Fixed-dimension factorization comparison
Systems with the same total Hilbert space dimension but different factorizations were compared:

| d_total | Factorization | R_ent | Purity fluctuations |
|---------|--------------|-------|-------------------|
| 12 | 2×6 | 0.4545 | var(γ) = 0.00564 |
| 12 | 3×4 | 0.5455 | var(γ) = 0.00630 |
| 16 | 2×8 | 0.4667 | var(γ) = 0.00358 |
| 16 | 4×4 | 0.6000 | var(γ) = 0.00409 |

Higher R_ent correlates with larger purity fluctuations at fixed total dimension.

#### 2. Fibonacci scaling analysis
For Fibonacci factorizations F(n) × F(n+1):

$$1 - R_{\text{ent}} \sim \sqrt{5}/\phi^{2n-1}$$

The decay rate per Fibonacci step is φ² ≈ 2.618, confirming the golden ratio structure.

#### 3. Confounds identified
Initial negative correlation between R_ent and thermalization rate was a confound: larger systems thermalize slower because of bigger Hilbert spaces, not because of entanglement structure. The correct test (v2, v3) controls for total dimension.

#### 4. Correct observable identified
Purity *fluctuations* (not thermalization rate) are the right observable. The variance of γ(t) around its equilibrium value correlates with R_ent at fixed total dimension.

### Assessment
The dimensional second law is a geometric theorem about Hilbert space structure. Whether it drives actual thermalization dynamics is a subtler question. The numerical evidence supports that R_ent predicts the *magnitude of fluctuations* but not the *rate* of approach to equilibrium.

---

## Session 6: Purity, Locality, and Conjugacy
**Transcript:** `2026-02-09-01-05-29-purity-locality-conjugacy-casimir.txt` (542K)
**Date:** February 9, 2026

### Central question: Is purity conjugate to Hamiltonian locality?

In classical mechanics, conjugate variables (q, p) satisfy Hamilton's equations. The question is whether quantum purity γ and some notion of "locality" form such a pair.

### Key findings:

#### 1. Purity gradient is purely local
$$\max|\langle \nabla\gamma, I_A \otimes B_j \rangle| = 4.16 \times 10^{-16}$$
$$\max|\langle \nabla\gamma, A_i \otimes I_B \rangle| = 14.7424$$

The purity gradient lives *entirely* in the A ⊗ I_B subspace. It has zero nonlocal component. This is exact (verified to machine precision).

#### 2. Purity is a Casimir invariant
γ is exactly invariant under local unitaries:
$$\max|\gamma(U_{\text{loc}}\psi) - \gamma(\psi)| = 3.00 \times 10^{-15}$$

Only nonlocal generators (V_int) change γ. This identifies purity as a **Casimir invariant** of the local symmetry group SU(d_A) × SU(d_B).

#### 3. Casimir-changing map has rank = budget dimension
For a 3×4 system (d=12):
- 120 nonlocal generators
- Joint rank of (γ̇, ṗ₃) map: always 2
- 118 nonlocal generators preserve ALL Casimirs
- Rank = min(d_A, d_B) - 1 = 2 = TEP budget dimension

This is the many-to-one conjugacy: 2 Casimirs ↔ 2 independent changing-directions, each with a 118-dimensional fiber of equivalent generators.

#### 4. Momentum at Schwarzschild radius
Computed the "momentum" conjugate to purity at the analog of the Schwarzschild radius (γ = 1/d). The divergence of the G-factor at this point corresponds to infinite "force" needed to push purity below the maximally mixed value.

---

## Session 7: Casimir Structure, SU(1,1), and Geometry
**Transcript:** `2026-02-09-04-16-07-casimir-conjugacy-su11-geometry.txt` (380K)
**Date:** February 9, 2026

### Critical correction: Casimir, not conjugacy

The previous session's "conjugacy" was corrected. Purity and higher moments are **Casimir invariants**, not symplectic conjugate pairs. Key distinction:
- Conjugate pairs: {q, p} = 1 (nonzero Poisson bracket)
- Casimir invariants: commute with everything in the symmetry algebra

Budget variables (γ, p₃) are Casimirs of the local unitary group — they label orbits, not canonical pairs.

### Grassmannian curvature test
Is purity the radial coordinate of the entanglement Grassmannian?

| System | su(n) dim | local | nonlocal | budget | ent_TEP |
|--------|-----------|-------|----------|--------|---------|
| 2×2 | 15 | 6 | 9 | 1 | 1 |
| 2×3 | 35 | 11 | 24 | 1 | 2 |
| 3×3 | 80 | 16 | 64 | 2 | 4 |
| 3×4 | 143 | 23 | 120 | 2 | 6 |

The budget dimension equals min(d_A, d_B) - 1, matching the number of independent spectral moments beyond p₁ = 1.

### Correlated Casimir evolution
Under generic nonlocal Hamiltonians, the Casimir changes (δγ, δp₃) are correlated but not deterministically linked — they share a 2-dimensional changing-subspace but individual trajectories explore it differently.

### SU(1,1) connection
The budget equation x² + u = 1 is the boundary of the Poincaré disk model of hyperbolic geometry. The SU(1,1) group acts naturally on this space:
- Boosts (Lorentz transformations) move along the radial direction
- Rotations act on the "phase" degree of freedom

Speed limits arise from the SU(1,1) Casimir.

### Spin-locking observation
Under evolution, total thermalization by one metric (e.g., eigenvalue equilibration) can protect coherence in a conjugate metric (e.g., eigenvector stability). This is analogous to Brownian spin-locking in NMR — the noise along one axis stabilizes the perpendicular component.

### Honest assessment of 118:2 ratio
The vast numerical dominance of purity-invisible over purity-visible channels corresponds to something well-known: **decoherence is faster than thermalization**. The 118 "phase" generators scramble eigenvector correlations (decoherence) while only 2 change eigenvalues (thermalization). This is a restatement, not a prediction.

# PHASE IV: SPECTRAL MOMENT HIERARCHY (Feb 13)

## Session 9: Purity Speed Limit Validation and Hierarchy Discovery
**Transcript:** `2026-02-13-01-07-32-purity-speed-limit-validation-hierarchy.txt` (223K)
**Date:** February 13, 2026

### Analytical validation against known models:

#### Heisenberg exchange (two qubits)
- J = 1.0, ‖V_int‖ = 0.75
- Speed limit: max(|γ̇|/bound) = 0.667
- Bound is **loose** — peak saturation at γ = 1.0 (product state) with ratio 2/3
- Zero violations across full trajectory

#### Jaynes-Cummings model (qubit + cavity)
- ω = 1.0, g = 0.2, N_cavity = 10
- Speed limit: max(|γ̇|/bound) = **1.201**
- **APPARENT VIOLATION** — bound exceeded by 20%

### Critical discovery: Factor-4 bound is dimension-dependent

The initial bound |γ̇| ≤ 4‖H‖√F used a constant prefactor of 4. This was shown to be exact only for d_A = 2 (qubits). For higher dimensions, the prefactor can exceed 4. The Jaynes-Cummings violation occurred because the cavity truncation creates an effective d_B > 2 system.

### Resolution: The exact Cauchy-Schwarz hierarchy

The correct, dimension-independent bound was derived:

$$\frac{dp_k}{dt} = k \cdot \sum_i \lambda_i^{k-1} \cdot \frac{d\lambda_i}{dt}$$

This is a **weighted Vandermonde system**: the rate of change of the k-th moment is determined by a linear combination of eigenvalue velocities, weighted by the (k-1)-th powers of the eigenvalues.

Verified to 10⁻¹⁷ precision.

### p₃ extraction protocol
A key practical contribution: from the dynamics of purity alone, one can extract the third spectral moment p₃ without performing full state tomography. The protocol:
1. Measure γ(t) at multiple times
2. Fit |γ̇(t)| as a function of γ(t)
3. The envelope of this fit constrains √(p₃ - γ²)

This is potentially the most novel practical result — it provides spectral information beyond purity from purity dynamics alone.

### Retraction
The factor-4 constant was retracted as non-universal. The correct bound involves the full weight matrix W, not just a scalar prefactor.

---

## Session 10: Teaching Session — Building Mathematical Fluency
**Transcript:** `2026-02-13-01-11-37-spectral-hierarchy-teaching-session.txt` (486K)
**Date:** February 13, 2026

Interactive session building fluency with:
- Cauchy-Schwarz inequality for matrices/operators
- Trace mechanics (cyclic property, partial trace)
- Product rule differentiation for matrix functions
- Vandermonde systems and their role in moment problems

A problem set PDF was generated for practice. The session also included strategic reasoning about how to frame the paper for maximum clarity.

### Key insight: "The constant is exactly 4, not 8/3"

For d_A = 2 (any d_B), the bound was proved analytically:

$$|\dot{\gamma}| = 4\sqrt{a(1-a)} \cdot |2a-1| \cdot |\text{Im}(A_{12} \cdot B_{21})|$$

where a is the larger Schmidt coefficient. The maximum over unit-norm A⊗B achieves |Im(A₁₂·B₂₁)| = 1. The identity 4√(a(1-a))·|2a-1| = 4√(p₃-γ²) holds exactly for two-level subsystems.

The JC model's ratio of 4/3 was **not** a violation — it was a non-rank-1 interaction that doesn't saturate the bound. The factor-4 bound is exact and tight for qubits.

### Tensor formulation: weighted Vandermonde
The moment rate equations form a weighted Vandermonde system:

$$\dot{p}_k = k \cdot \sum_i \lambda_i^{k-1} \cdot \dot{\lambda}_i$$

Defining M_{ki} = k·λᵢᵏ⁻¹, the system dp/dt = M · dλ/dt has the Vandermonde structure, which is invertible when eigenvalues are distinct. This means: given the rates of change of enough moments, one can reconstruct the eigenvalue velocities.

## Sessions 11–12: Literature Review
**Transcripts:** `2026-02-13-21-09-56-literature-review-novelty-assessment.txt` (94K), `2026-02-13-23-05-46-spectral-hierarchy-literature-tep-critique.txt` (106K)
**Date:** February 13, 2026

### Bensa & Žnidarič comparison
Paper: "Fastest Local Entanglement Scrambler, Multistage Thermalization, and a Non-Hermitian Phantom"

Key distinctions from our work:
- **Their framework:** Average purity decay I(t) = ⟨Tr(ρ_A²)⟩ in random quantum circuits, mapped to Markovian transfer matrix. Rate r_E is asymptotic exponential decay.
- **Our framework:** Instantaneous rate |dγ/dt| for a specific state under deterministic Hamiltonian. No averaging, no circuits.

Structural parallel identified: both frameworks say "spectral information at a given order is insufficient to predict dynamics at that order." Their phantom eigenvalue phenomenon (where expansion coefficients blow up, making |λ₂| fail to predict the rate) mirrors our finding that γ alone doesn't predict |γ̇| — you need p₃.

### Non-Markovianity and channel additivity (first appearance)
The three-regime structure of non-Markovian advantage was identified:
1. **Short probe separation:** Information from first probe indistinguishable from channel fluctuations. Advantage: zero.
2. **Intermediate separation:** Perturbation has created structured correlations that entangled second probe can access. Advantage: maximal.
3. **Large separation:** Perturbation fully thermalized. Channel healed. Advantage: zero.

This non-monotonic profile would later connect to the thin-film correspondence.

**Date:** February 13, 2026

### Six core results assessed for novelty:

| Result | Novelty | Risk |
|--------|---------|------|
| Spectral moment hierarchy dp_k/dt = Vandermonde | Likely novel in this form | Low — clean algebra |
| p₃ extraction from purity dynamics | Potentially novel | Medium — may exist in QSL literature |
| Tight purity speed limit via F = p₃ - γ² | Novel framing, possibly known mechanism | High — need to check Pires, Hamazaki |
| Rank-2 structure of W | Likely novel | Low — algebraic |
| Iso-purity variation (F independent of γ) | Novel as explicit result | Low |
| Channel additivity connection | Highly speculative | Very high |

### Competing work identified:
- **Shrimali & Pati (2024):** Stronger speed limits for observables, including capacity of entanglement
- **Bensa & Žnidarič (2021):** Random circuit purity decay rates
- **Hartmann et al.:** Short-time purity bounds

### Non-Markovianity insight deepened
The connection between channel memory structure and additivity was developed further:
- A perfectly Markovian (memoryless) channel gets zero benefit from entangled inputs — additivity holds trivially
- A channel with rich internal structure permits but doesn't require entangled inputs to unlock additional capacity
- The non-additivity gap measures the channel's *susceptibility* to entanglement, not entanglement's intrinsic power
- The peak advantage location is determined by the channel's internal correlation time

# PHASE V: GMC-PURITY IDENTIFICATION AND TRANS-CRITICAL ANALYSIS (Feb 14)

## Session 14: TEP-GMC Dictionary
**Transcript:** `2026-02-14-03-54-23-tep-gmc-purity-budget-identification.txt` (576K)
**Date:** February 14, 2026

### Resolving the gamma confusion

Three different "gammas" had been conflated:
1. **γ_purity = Tr(ρ²):** Quantum purity of the reduced state
2. **γ_GMC:** Intermittency parameter of Gaussian Multiplicative Chaos
3. **γ_Lyapunov:** Lyapunov exponent in chaotic dynamics

### The correct TEP-GMC dictionary:

$$u = D_\gamma = 1 - \gamma_{\text{GMC}}^2/2$$
$$x^2 = 1 - u = \gamma_{\text{GMC}}^2/2$$

So the budget equation x² + u = 1 **is** the GMC Fourier dimension formula — not imposed as an axiom but inherited from multiplicative chaos structure.

### Hartmann short-time bound mapping
Hartmann gives γ_purity(t) ≈ 1 - (t/τ)² at short times. The GMC identification maps this to:

$$\gamma_{\text{GMC}} = \sqrt{2} \cdot t/\tau$$

This is a specific claim: physical time evolution maps to the intermittency parameter of a multiplicative chaos, with purity playing the role of Fourier dimension.

### SU(1,1) hyperbolic geometry connection
The budget constraint x² + u = 1 is the boundary of the Poincaré disk. The dynamics live in the interior, with:
- x = tanh(η/2) where η is the hyperbolic rapidity
- The SU(1,1) Casimir constrains the accessible trajectories
- Sub-additivity of entropy corresponds to the triangle inequality in hyperbolic geometry

## Session 15: Trans-Critical Regime
**Transcript:** `2026-02-14-09-21-01-trans-critical-gmc-purity-analysis.txt` (177K)
**Date:** February 14, 2026

### Hierarchy of horizons

For a d_A-dimensional subsystem, there are d_A - 1 "horizons" at:

$$x_k = \sqrt{1 - 1/k} \quad \text{for } k = 2, \ldots, d_A$$

The first horizon x₂ = 1/√2 (corresponding to γ = 1/2) is the metric crossover point for qubits.

### Trans-critical regime
For qutrits and higher: the range x₂ < x < x_{d_A} represents a regime where the system has "crossed" the qubit horizon but not reached its own dimensional limit. In this regime:
- G(x) diverges relative to the qubit metric
- But the qutrit metric is still well-behaved
- The spectral structure has qualitatively different character

### Key verification
The G-factor formula F = x²/G²(x) was verified to exact numerical agreement across all dimensions:

| t | x | √2·x | F_exact | F_Gfactor | match |
|---|---|-------|---------|-----------|-------|
| 0.0 | 0.000 | 0.000 | 0.000000 | 0.000000 | YES |
| 0.1 | 0.140 | 0.199 | 0.009478 | 0.009478 | YES |
| ... | ... | ... | ... | ... | YES |

For qubits, √2·x never exceeds 1 — the qubit horizon is never crossed. For qutrits, x can exceed 1/√2, entering the trans-critical regime.

## Session 16: Iso-Purity Tests and G-Factor Paths
**Transcript:** `2026-02-14-09-27-09-iso-purity-test-g-factor-paths.txt` (325K)
**Date:** February 14, 2026

### Eigenvalue horizons as dimensional relevance thresholds

The horizon at x_k corresponds to the threshold where the k-th eigenvalue becomes/ceases to be relevant. In spectral terms: when the system crosses x_k, the k-th eigenvalue is either entering or leaving the "active" part of the spectrum.

This gives a physical interpretation: **horizons are thresholds beyond which a degree of freedom becomes or ceases to be dynamically relevant.**

### Iso-purity manifold structure
At fixed γ, varying the eigenvalue distribution traces out the iso-purity manifold. On this manifold:
- F varies (different transport capacity at same purity)
- von Neumann entropy S varies
- Higher moments p₃, p₄, ... vary

The iso-purity manifold is the "hidden" degree of freedom invisible to purity measurements alone — the fiber over a point in purity space.

# PHASE VI: FISHER GEOMETRY AND RANK-2 DISCOVERY (Feb 14, evening)

## Session 17: Purity Bound Tightness
**Transcript:** `2026-02-14-21-24-28-purity-bound-tightness-classical-quantum.txt` (175K)
**Date:** February 14, 2026 (evening)

### The "classical dynamics" puzzle

The optimal Hamiltonian for purity change only has nonzero matrix elements at positions (a,ã)-(c,c̃) in the Schmidt basis — coupling |a⟩_A|ã⟩_B to |c⟩_A|c̃⟩_B where ã, c̃ are the corresponding Schmidt partners.

This raised a concern: "If the derivative of a classical state is classical, isn't the evolved state also classical?"

### Resolution
The eigenbasis of ρ_A is *always* diagonal in the eigenbasis — that's tautological. The dynamics move eigenvalues while rotating the eigenbasis. The optimal H changes eigenvalues maximally while minimizing eigenvector rotation. This is not "classical" — it's the most efficient use of quantum resources for the specific task of purity transport.

---

## Session 18: Fisher Geometry and Rank-2 Structure
**Transcript:** `2026-02-14-21-41-40-fisher-geometry-rank2-time-dilation.txt` (364K)
**Date:** February 14, 2026 (evening)

### THIS IS THE CENTRAL DISCOVERY SESSION.

### Result 1: The algebraic identity F = p₃ - p₂²

Proved (dimension-independent):

$$F = \sum_{a<c} \lambda_a \lambda_c (\lambda_a - \lambda_c)^2 = p_3 - p_2^2 = p_3 - \gamma^2$$

Verified numerically for d = 2, 3, 4, 5 with exact agreement.

### Result 2: F = ¼‖∇γ‖²_Fisher

The quantity F is exactly one-quarter of the squared Fisher information gradient of purity:

$$F = \frac{1}{4}\|\nabla\gamma\|^2_{\text{Fisher}}$$

Verified:

| d_A | F | ‖∇γ‖²_Fisher/4 | ratio |
|-----|---|-----------------|-------|
| 2 | 0.05197 | 0.05197 | 1.0000000000 |
| 3 | 0.01560 | 0.01560 | 1.0000000000 |
| 4 | 0.00823 | 0.00823 | 1.0000000000 |
| 5 | 0.00491 | 0.00491 | 1.0000000000 |

### Result 3: W is rank-2 in ALL dimensions

The weight bivector W_{ac} = √(λ_a λ_c)(λ_a - λ_c) is **always rank-2** as an antisymmetric matrix, regardless of d_A ≥ 2.

For d_A = 3: W lives in R³ (three pairs: 01, 02, 12). The rank-2 antisymmetric matrix in R³ spans a single plane — the u-v plane.

For d_A ≥ 4: W lives in R^(d(d-1)/2), but the algebraic structure forces it to remain rank-2. This was the unexpected result — the constraint comes from the fact that W_{ac} factorizes as the product of two vectors:

$$W_{ac} = u_a v_c - u_c v_a$$

where u_a = √λ_a · λ_a and v_a = √λ_a. This is a single wedge product, hence rank-2.

### Result 4: Tight bound with constructive saturating Hamiltonian

$$\left|\frac{d\gamma}{dt}\right| \leq 4\|H\|\sqrt{F}$$

with equality achieved by:

$$H_{\text{opt}} = \frac{iW}{\sqrt{F}}$$

This is a rank-2 antisymmetric matrix — the generator of rotation in exactly one plane.

### Result 5: Two-factor time dilation

$$\tau_\gamma = \underbrace{\frac{1}{4\sqrt{F}}}_{\text{geometric inertia}} \cdot \underbrace{\frac{1}{\|H\|}}_{\text{dynamical timescale}}$$

The purity evolution timescale factorizes exactly into a geometric piece (depending only on the state) and a dynamical piece (depending only on the Hamiltonian).

### Result 6: F has a variational principle

F = ¼‖∇γ‖²_Fisher means F can be obtained by maximizing the purity rate over all unit-norm Hamiltonians:

$$F = \frac{1}{16} \max_{\|H\|=1} \left(\frac{d\gamma}{dt}\right)^2$$

This is a clean variational characterization.

### Assessment given at this point:
"The core result — tight purity speed limit, explicit saturating Hamiltonian, rank-2 mechanism — is a solid, correct piece of mathematics at the level of a short paper or letter in a specialized journal. Think Physical Review A, Journal of Physics A, or Quantum."

# PHASE VII: CHANNEL ADDITIVITY AND THIN-FILM CORRESPONDENCE (Feb 14–15)

## Session 19: Rank-2 Simplification and Additivity Connection
**Transcript:** `2026-02-15-01-41-06-rank2-simplification-additivity-connection.txt` (185K)
**Date:** February 14–15, 2026

### Budget decomposition of the bound

The saturation gap (why most Hamiltonians don't saturate the bound) decomposes into:
1. **Angular misalignment (α):** The Hamiltonian doesn't point along the optimal direction in the weight space
2. **Norm leakage (η):** Some of ‖H‖ is "wasted" on purity-invisible modes

Both factors contribute multiplicatively: actual rate = bound × cos(α) × η.

### Connection to channel additivity (first explicit statement)

The Hastings (2009) counterexample disproved the minimum output entropy additivity conjecture: there exist channels Φ₁, Φ₂ where:

$$S_{\min}(\Phi_1 \otimes \Phi_2) < S_{\min}(\Phi_1) + S_{\min}(\Phi_2)$$

Entangled inputs can beat product inputs. But the size of the gap was not bounded.

The TEP connection: the rank-2 transport structure might provide a geometric bound on this gap, because:
- The output purity is constrained by the transport plane W
- The angle θ between u and v determines how much of p₃ appears as purity vs. transport capacity
- At the metric balance point γ* = 2 - √2, this angle is maximally informative

---

## Session 20: Metric Competition and Additivity
**Transcript:** `2026-02-15-01-42-10-metric-competition-additivity-rank2-connection.txt` (292K)
**Date:** February 15, 2026

### Clarification of research motivation

The original motivation was not the speed limit per se, but the **sub-, super-, and strong-subadditivity regimes** characterized by competition between the purity metric and Bures metric, with the triangle inequality governing channel additivity.

### Hastings gap assessment
"Hastings' proof is probabilistic — it shows violations exist but gives no tight bound on the gap. The counterexamples have very high dimension (d > 10⁵) and very small gaps. No one knows the maximum possible gap."

The conjecture: the rank-2 transport structure at the metric balance point provides a geometric bound on this gap.

## Session 21: Channel Additivity and Thin-Film Correspondence (THE CENTRAL SESSION)
**Transcript:** `2026-02-15-07-41-32-quantum-channel-additivity-thin-film-correspondence.txt` (525K, 2192 lines)
**Date:** February 14–15, 2026

### The θ decomposition

The angle θ between the position vector u and gradient vector v in the transport plane:

$$\gamma = \sqrt{p_3} \cdot \cos\theta$$
$$F = p_3 \cdot \sin^2\theta$$
$$\gamma^2 + F = p_3 \quad \text{(Pythagorean)}$$

cos θ controls how much of p₃ is "visible as purity" (cos²θ) versus "available as transport capacity" (sin²θ).

### Three regimes of quantum channel behavior

**Regime 1: cos θ ≈ 1 (Sub-additive)**
- Nearly all of p₃ appears as purity
- u and v are nearly aligned — redundant measurement
- Two probes see the same information
- Channel output entropy satisfies the triangle inequality comfortably
- Product inputs are optimal → additivity holds

**Regime 2: cos θ at critical angle (Strong sub-additivity boundary)**
- Metric competition between purity and Bures geometries maximized
- The additivity gap is most constrained here
- This is the balance point γ* = 2 - √2

**Regime 3: cos θ ≈ 0 (Super-additive)**
- Nearly all of p₃ appears as transport capacity F
- u and v are orthogonal — independent information
- Entangled inputs can beat product inputs
- Additivity is violated

### The thin-film optical correspondence

The three-regime structure maps precisely onto thin-film optics:

| Quantum | Thin Film |
|---------|-----------|
| cos θ (u-v alignment) | cos θᵢ (angle of incidence) |
| Sub-additive regime | Normal incidence: 1+r=t, max absorption 50% |
| Balance point | Brewster angle: reflected wave vanishes for one polarization |
| Super-additive regime | Grazing incidence: total reflection |
| Rank-2 bivector W | Electromagnetic field tensor F^μν (also rank-2) |
| Purity-visible/invisible modes | Two polarization states (s and p) |

The Brewster angle in optics is the angle where the reflected wave vanishes for p-polarization — the competition between electric and magnetic boundary conditions reaches its extremum. This is the structural analog of the metric balance point where purity and Bures curvatures cross.

### Maximum absorption = 50% at normal incidence
In thin-film optics, a single absorbing film at normal incidence can absorb at most 50% of incident energy — this is a fundamental limit from the tangential field boundary condition 1 + r = t. The quantum analog: in the sub-additive regime, the maximum "information extraction" from a single channel use is bounded by the same geometric structure.

### The bivector as rotation generator

W is a plane of rotation, not merely a plane:
- The optimal Hamiltonian H_opt = iW/√F is antisymmetric
- Exponentiation gives rotation: e^{-iHt} rotates in the u-v plane
- There is exactly one plane of rotation (rank-2)
- All other planes preserve purity

This is the direct analog of the electromagnetic field tensor F^μν, which is also rank-2 and encodes the plane of electromagnetic rotation (E and B as components of a single bivector).

### The additivity gap conjecture

**Conjecture:** The additivity gap for quantum channels is bounded by 2√2 - 2 ≈ 0.828.

This would arise from the rank-2 transport structure at the metric balance point:
- At γ* = 2 - √2: x² = 2√2 - 2, u = 3 - 2√2
- These values are in Z[√2], connecting to silver ratio and octagonal symmetry
- The bound would be a geometric consequence of the rank-2 constraint

### Assessment of significance:
"If you could prove that the additivity gap for quantum channels is bounded by 2√2 − 2, with the bound arising from the rank-2 transport structure at the metric balance point — that would be a major result in quantum information theory."

But: "This remains a conjecture requiring formalization."

### Scope of universality

The bound |dγ/dt| ≤ 4‖H‖√F applies to **all Hamiltonian (unitary) evolution** on any bipartite system of any dimension. It uses only the von Neumann equation, spectral decomposition of ρ_A, and algebraic structure of W. No assumptions about H, dimensions, initial state, or interaction type.

On measurements: a projective measurement doesn't transport purity faster than the bound — it **destroys one system and creates another**. The bound applies within each unitary segment.

On effective non-unitarity: non-unitary dynamics from a subsystem perspective are always unitary from the total system perspective. The bound holds given proper renormalization.

### Purity-invisible modes as thermodynamic channels

The (d-2)-dimensional orthogonal complement of W contains all purity-preserving rotations. These change F, higher moments, and entropy without changing γ. They are the modes by which a system can thermalize (change entropy, redistribute correlations) while appearing static from the purity perspective.

This gives the bound an equivalent representation as a **limit on the rate of thermalization** given F and γ.

### Pythagorean decomposition of spectral velocity

$$\left\|\frac{d\boldsymbol{\lambda}}{dt}\right\|^2 = (\text{purity-visible rate})^2 + (\text{purity-invisible rate})^2$$

Both share a total budget bounded by ‖H‖². Maximizing purity change minimizes invisible change, and vice versa.

### Publication strategy recommended:

**Stage 1 (ready now):** Tight purity speed limit paper. Self-contained: |dγ/dt| ≤ 4‖H‖√F, rank-2 W, saturating H, Fisher gradient identity, time dilation factorization. No TEP references. Frame as quantum information geometry.

**Stage 2 (pending formalization):** Channel additivity paper. Requires proving the gap bound from rank-2 structure.

# PHASE VIII: HOLONOMY TESTING AND FALSIFICATION (Feb 15 morning)

## Session 22: Holonomy and Entropy Surprise
**Transcript:** `2026-02-15-08-36-57-holonomy-test-entropy-surprise.txt` (292K)
**Date:** February 15, 2026

### Fiber bundle simulation

Built a comprehensive qutrit × qutrit bipartite simulation testing:
1. Rank-2 transport decomposition (visible vs. invisible)
2. Holonomy in purity cycles (does F return when γ returns?)
3. Statistical correlations on iso-purity manifold

### The F–S correlation surprise

On the iso-purity manifold (fixed γ), F and von Neumann entropy S are **positively correlated with near-unit correlation**:

| γ | Correlation(F, S) |
|---|-------------------|
| 0.40 | 0.9999 |
| 0.50 | ~0.999 |
| 0.60 | ~0.999 |

This means: states with high transport capacity (high F) also have high entropy. States with low F have spectra closer to "flat" within the iso-purity constraint.

This was **unexpected** and challenges the naive interpretation that high-F states are "far from equilibrium" — they can be far from equilibrium in terms of purity while being close to maximum entropy within their purity class.

## Session 23: Holonomy Falsification and Factor-of-2
**Transcript:** `2026-02-15-08-39-02-holonomy-falsification-settling-normalization.txt` (497K)
**Date:** February 15, 2026

### The factor-of-2 violation

A single apparent violation was found in qutrit × ququart (d_A=3, d_B=4) at ratio ~2.02. Investigation:

- Did **not** reproduce across 10,000 trials
- The ratio ≈ 2 is suspicious — a random numerical artifact would give a much larger or smaller ratio
- Resolution: the violation occurred at **purity = 1.0** (product state), making the ratio 0/0 → indeterminate

### Schmidt-basis normalization correction
The original bound formula assumed a specific normalization of the coupling matrix elements. When the bound was re-derived in the Schmidt basis with correct normalization:

$$\frac{d\gamma}{dt} = -4 \sum_{a<c} W_{ac} \cdot \text{Im}(h_{ac})$$

where h_{ac} = ⟨a,ã|H_{AB}|c,c̃⟩ are Schmidt-basis matrix elements, all violations vanished.

### Post-return evolution
After a purity-returning holonomic cycle:
- ΔF ≠ 0 (F does **not** return to its initial value)
- ΔS ≠ 0 (entropy changes)
- This is a genuine geometric phase effect on the purity manifold

## Sessions 25–27: Holonomy Entropy Production and Critical Assessment
**Transcripts:** Multiple sessions (Feb 15, ~08:30–09:45)

### Entropy production during holonomic paths

High-resolution continuous tracking of dS/dt, dF/dt, dγ/dt across all phases of a purity-returning cycle:

| Phase | γ | dS/dt | dF/dt |
|-------|---|-------|-------|
| Pre-cycle | 0.65 | ~0 | ~0 |
| Leg 1 (depurify) | decreasing | positive | varies |
| Leg 2 (repurify) | increasing | negative* | varies |
| Return (γ back to 0.65) | 0.65 | nonzero | nonzero |
| Post-cycle | settling | → 0 | → 0 |

*The negative dS/dt during repurification was initially surprising but is consistent: entropy can decrease in a subsystem when the subsystem re-entangles with its complement.

### F-relevance critical assessment

After discovering degenerate initial state bias, tested whether foundational claims survive with generic spectra:
- Algebraic identity F = p₃ - γ²: **survives** (it's an identity, not statistical)
- Rank-2 structure: **survives** (algebraic)
- Bound tightness: **survives** (constructive)
- F as predictive of dynamics beyond γ: **weakened** — partial correlations show F adds moderate but not dramatic predictive power beyond γ alone for generic states

### The settling interpretation
After a holonomic cycle, the system's *base-space* coordinates (γ) return but the *fiber-space* coordinates (F, S, higher moments) don't. Over longer times, the fiber variables relax toward their equilibrium values at the given γ — but this relaxation is controlled by the purity-invisible modes, not the purity-visible transport.

This cleanly separates two thermodynamic processes:
1. **Base-space (decoherence) thermodynamics:** Purity approaches equilibrium, governed by W
2. **Fiber-space (spectral) thermodynamics:** Higher moments approach their equilibrium values at given γ, governed by the W-orthogonal complement

# APPENDIX B: Key Equations Reference

### Budget constraint
$$x^2 + u = 1 \qquad G(x) = \frac{1}{\sqrt{1-x^2}}$$

### Spectral moments
$$p_k = \text{Tr}(\rho_A^k) = \sum_i \lambda_i^k$$

### Fisher information of purity
$$F = p_3 - p_2^2 = \sum_{a<c} \lambda_a \lambda_c (\lambda_a - \lambda_c)^2 = \frac{1}{4}\|\nabla\gamma\|^2_{\text{Fisher}}$$

### Weight bivector
$$W_{ac} = \sqrt{\lambda_a \lambda_c}(\lambda_a - \lambda_c) = u_a v_c - u_c v_a \quad \text{(rank-2)}$$

### Tight purity speed limit
$$\left|\frac{d\gamma}{dt}\right| \leq 4\|H\|\sqrt{F} \qquad \text{achieved by } H_{\text{opt}} = \frac{iW}{\sqrt{F}}$$

### θ decomposition
$$\gamma = \sqrt{p_3}\cos\theta \qquad F = p_3\sin^2\theta \qquad \gamma^2 + F = p_3$$

### Moment rate hierarchy (Vandermonde)
$$\frac{dp_k}{dt} = k \sum_i \lambda_i^{k-1} \frac{d\lambda_i}{dt}$$

### Two-factor time dilation
$$\tau_\gamma = \frac{1}{4\sqrt{F}} \cdot \frac{1}{\|H\|}$$

### Entanglement dimension ratio
$$R_{\text{ent}} = \frac{(d_A-1)(d_B-1)}{d_A d_B - 1}$$

### Hierarchy of horizons
$$x_k = \sqrt{1 - \frac{1}{k}} \qquad k = 2, \ldots, d_A$$

### Critical purity (d=2)
$$\gamma^* = 2 - \sqrt{2} \approx 0.5858 \qquad x^{*2} = 2\sqrt{2}-2 \qquad u^* = 3 - 2\sqrt{2}$$

### Additivity gap conjecture
$$\Delta S_{\min} \leq 2\sqrt{2} - 2 \approx 0.828$$

### Lyapunov-capacity theorem (from earlier work)
$$\frac{d(C/B)}{dt} = -\frac{\lambda_L}{\ln 2}$$
```

```plaintext
# hi 3


**User - --**


Hi! attached is a theoretical framework. Apologies for the redundant intro; please rigorously consider the attached transcript -- sources included -- as though you are a review panelist for a competitive journal, sharing your honest assessment in private with a colleague at or above your own level of theoretical grasp.
```
